The Third Type of Guidance: Hidayat al-Tawfiq
Definition of the third type of guidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Hidayat al-Tawfiq as conditional divine grace that depends on human choice, and distinguish it from deterministic views.

Core Idea
Divine guidance is a reward for choice, not coercion.

In this passage, the author defines the third type of guidance, called Hidayat al-Tawfiq. He emphasizes that this guidance is not deterministic but rather a grace or anger contingent on the servant's actions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for reconciling divine predestination with human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the phrase 'النوع الثالث : الإيصال إلى المطلوب' in the Arabic. Note that it is also called 'هداية التوفيق'.
This is the definiendum.
2
Extract the nature of this guidance
The author says it is 'لطف أو غضب' (grace or anger) from Allah. This implies it is a response to human actions, not arbitrary.
3
Analyze the condition for receiving it
According to the author, it is received by those who 'سلك طريقا صالحا باختياره' (take a righteous path by choice). This shows it is conditional.
The condition is human choice and effort.
4
Contrast with coercion
The author argues that this guidance does not imply compulsion; rather, it is compatible with free will. He states that the superficial reading of the verse might suggest determinism, but the deeper meaning is honor or punishment based on choice.
This sets up the later argument against coercion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث : الإيصال إلى المطلوب : وتسمى أيضا هداية التوفيق وهي لطف أو غضب من الله سبحانه قال عز من قائل (اللهَ يُضِلُّ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ) ۳ ان اللطف أو الغضب الالهي على العبد لا يعني ان الانسان مجبر لا يمتلك الخيار لان الهداية والاضلال من الله كما توحي القراءة الظاهرية السطحية للآية ( ان الانسان كائن مفكر مختار ومركز إهتدائه أو ضلالته هو قلبه لان سائر قواه وأعضاء بدنه بمنزلة الآلات المطيعة لقلبه وان الهداية والاضلال نوع من التكريم أو العقاب الذي يقرره الله سبحانه يشمل كل من سلك طريقا صالحا باختياره فيوصله الله إلى الفوز ويحافظ عليه ولا يوقعه في الضلال وهذه الهداية لا مانع منها عقلاً وعقلائياً ولا تزاحم عدل الله تعالى لأنها بالرغم من اشتراطها بالسعي والثبات فهي شاملة لجميع الخلق من غير تخصيص أما من حرم نفسه من اللطف بعمله السيئ فوقع في الظلمات فلا يلومن إلا نفسه ولو كانت الهداية والاضلال بمعنى الاجبار على الضلال أو الهدى أو إمالة القلب من الحق الى الباطل كما يزعم البعض فان هذا يتقاطع مع العدل الالهي فالهداية لا تقع من دون سبب وخلاف الحكمة الإلهية ) والَّذِينَ اهْتَدَوا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى وَآتَاهُمْ تَقْوَاهُمْ " إن المراد ليس هو إيجاد الهداية بطريق جبري وقسري وتكويني بل انزال العقاب أو اللطف إن هذه الهداية على قسمين : أ : الايصال الى المطلوب في الدنيا : وهو تكريم أو توبيخ يختص به الله بعض العباد كما في قوله تعالى( وَالَّذِينَ جَاهَدُوا فِينا لنهدينهم سبلنا ) فهي هداية تتعلق بالمكاسب فمن كسب العبد وهى مسبوقة ففى قوله تعالى (والذين جاهدوا فينا) (يَهْدِي به اللَّهُ مَن اتَّبَعَ رِضْوَانَهُ سُبُلَ السَّلَام وَيُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ بِإِذْنِهِ وَيَهْدِيهِمْ إِلَى صراط مستقيم ( ٤ ) فهي من هذا الوجه نعمة منه سبحانه عليهم ومنة منه واصلة إليهم وفضل منه وإحسان لديهم وقد يكون الايصال الى المطلوب الهداية في القرآن عبدالله جواد ،آملي، ط1، دار الهادي، بيروت، ١٩٩٣م، ص ٥٧ ٢ سورة محمد الآية ١٧ ٣ سورة العنكبوت الآية ٦٩ ٤ سورة المائدة الآية ١٦
The third type: Bringing to the desired, also called guidance of tawfiq (success), and it is grace or anger from Allah Almighty. He said, Glorified and Exalted: 'Allah leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills.' Indeed, divine grace or anger upon the servant does not mean that man is compelled and has no choice, because guidance and misguidance are from Allah, as the superficial apparent reading of the verse suggests. Rather, man is a thinking, choosing being, and the center of his guidance or misguidance is his heart, for all his powers and bodily organs are like obedient instruments to his heart. Guidance and misguidance are a type of honor or punishment that Allah decrees, encompassing everyone who takes a righteous path by his choice, so Allah brings him to success and preserves him and does not let him fall into misguidance. There is no rational or societal impediment to this guidance, nor does it conflict with Allah's justice because despite its condition of striving and steadfastness, it encompasses all of creation without specification. As for one who deprives himself of grace through his evil actions and falls into darkness, he has only himself to blame. If guidance and misguidance were in the sense of compulsion towards misguidance or guidance, or turning the heart from truth to falsehood, as some claim, then this would contradict divine justice. Guidance does not occur without a cause and contrary to divine wisdom. 'And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance and gives them their piety.' The intent is not to create guidance in a coercive, forceful, and ontological way, but rather to send down punishment or grace. This guidance is of two kinds: A: Bringing to the desired in this world: it is honor or reprimand that Allah bestows upon some servants, as in His statement: 'And those who strive for Us, We will surely guide them to Our ways.' So it is guidance related to gains. What the servant earns is preceded by... (The passage continues with another verse and commentary).
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage defines the third type of guidance, which is 'bringing to the desired' (الإيصال إلى المطلوب), also called the guidance of success (هداية التوفيق). The author first states that this guidance is an act of divine grace or anger, citing the verse that Allah guides whom He wills and leads astray whom He wills. However, the author immediately clarifies that this does not imply human compulsion. He argues that a superficial reading might suggest determinism, but in truth, man is a free-thinking being whose heart is the center of guidance. The guidance of tawfiq is a reward or punishment based on one's choices. It is rationally and socially acceptable and does not contradict divine justice because it is conditional upon striving and steadfastness. If someone deprives himself of grace through his bad deeds, he is to blame. The author then critiques the view that guidance and misguidance are coercive, stating that such a view would nullify divine justice. Finally, he subdivides this third type into two: guidance in this world, which is a form of honor or reprimand for certain servants, citing the verse about striving for Allah.

Key Terms
هداية التوفيق
الإيصال إلى المطلوب
الهداية والاضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the relationship between divine guidance of tawfiq and human free will?
A) Guidance is completely coercive
B) Guidance is conditional upon human choice and effort
C) Guidance and misguidance are random
D) Human will has no role in guidance

Key Takeaway
Hidayat al-Tawfiq is a conditional divine grace that honors or punishes based on human choice, not a deterministic decree.

5 min
The Logical Argument against Coercive Guidance
Refutation of coercive guidance using modus tollens

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's argument that coercive guidance contradicts divine justice, using the conditional logic form of modus tollens.

Core Idea
If guidance were coercive, God would be unjust; but God is just, so guidance is not coercive.

The author anticipates a potential objection: that verses like 'Allah leads astray whom He wills' imply determinism. He responds with a logical argument: if guidance were coercive, it would violate divine justice. This lesson unpacks that argument and formalizes it as a conditional syllogism (modus tollens).

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
The claim is that guidance and misguidance are coercive (بمعنى الاجبار على الضلال أو الهدى), i.e., Allah forces people into belief or disbelief.
This is the opposite of the author's position.
2
Find the conditional premise
The author states: 'ولو كانت الهداية والاضلال بمعنى الاجبار على الضلال أو الهدى أو إمالة القلب من الحق الى الباطل كما يزعم البعض فان هذا يتقاطع مع العدل الالهي' (If guidance and misguidance were coercive, then this would contradict divine justice).
This is the major premise: if P then Q.
3
Identify the implied minor premise
The author takes for granted that Allah is just (العدل الالهي is established). This implies that the consequent (contradicting divine justice) is false.
In modus tollens, we deny the consequent: not Q.
4
Derive the conclusion
Therefore, guidance and misguidance are not coercive. The author implicitly concludes that the antecedent is false.
This is the conclusion: not P.
5
Test the logic
This is a valid modus tollens: If P then Q; not Q; therefore not P. The argument is logically sound.
The author does not explicitly state the minor premise, but it is implied by the belief in divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث : الإيصال إلى المطلوب : وتسمى أيضا هداية التوفيق وهي لطف أو غضب من الله سبحانه قال عز من قائل (اللهَ يُضِلُّ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ) ۳ ان اللطف أو الغضب الالهي على العبد لا يعني ان الانسان مجبر لا يمتلك الخيار لان الهداية والاضلال من الله كما توحي القراءة الظاهرية السطحية للآية ( ان الانسان كائن مفكر مختار ومركز إهتدائه أو ضلالته هو قلبه لان سائر قواه وأعضاء بدنه بمنزلة الآلات المطيعة لقلبه وان الهداية والاضلال نوع من التكريم أو العقاب الذي يقرره الله سبحانه يشمل كل من سلك طريقا صالحا باختياره فيوصله الله إلى الفوز ويحافظ عليه ولا يوقعه في الضلال وهذه الهداية لا مانع منها عقلاً وعقلائياً ولا تزاحم عدل الله تعالى لأنها بالرغم من اشتراطها بالسعي والثبات فهي شاملة لجميع الخلق من غير تخصيص أما من حرم نفسه من اللطف بعمله السيئ فوقع في الظلمات فلا يلومن إلا نفسه ولو كانت الهداية والاضلال بمعنى الاجبار على الضلال أو الهدى أو إمالة القلب من الحق الى الباطل كما يزعم البعض فان هذا يتقاطع مع العدل الالهي فالهداية لا تقع من دون سبب وخلاف الحكمة الإلهية ) والَّذِينَ اهْتَدَوا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى وَآتَاهُمْ تَقْوَاهُمْ " إن المراد ليس هو إيجاد الهداية بطريق جبري وقسري وتكويني بل انزال العقاب أو اللطف إن هذه الهداية على قسمين : أ : الايصال الى المطلوب في الدنيا : وهو تكريم أو توبيخ يختص به الله بعض العباد كما في قوله تعالى( وَالَّذِينَ جَاهَدُوا فِينا لنهدينهم سبلنا ) فهي هداية تتعلق بالمكاسب فمن كسب العبد وهى مسبوقة ففى قوله تعالى (والذين جاهدوا فينا) (يَهْدِي به اللَّهُ مَن اتَّبَعَ رِضْوَانَهُ سُبُلَ السَّلَام وَيُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ بِإِذْنِهِ وَيَهْدِيهِمْ إِلَى صراط مستقيم ( ٤ ) فهي من هذا الوجه نعمة منه سبحانه عليهم ومنة منه واصلة إليهم وفضل منه وإحسان لديهم وقد يكون الايصال الى المطلوب الهداية في القرآن عبدالله جواد ،آملي، ط1، دار الهادي، بيروت، ١٩٩٣م، ص ٥٧ ٢ سورة محمد الآية ١٧ ٣ سورة العنكبوت الآية ٦٩ ٤ سورة المائدة الآية ١٦

Commentary

Special Divine Teaching: Prophetic Knowledge and al-‘Ilm al-Ladunī
Author classifies divine teaching into special and general types with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two forms of special divine teaching (prophetic knowledge and iṣṭifā’) and distinguish them from general divine teaching.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge comes directly to prophets and the elect through ladunī and iṣṭifā’.

The Quran reveals that not all knowledge is acquired by human effort. This lesson explores the special divine teaching granted to prophets and select righteous individuals, including the concept of al-‘ilm al-ladunī and the process of iṣṭifā’. We will examine Quranic evidence and understand the purpose of this special teaching.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of divine teaching
The passage opens by stating that divine teaching is of two types: special and general. Special teaching is for an elite, especially prophets.
2
Recall Quranic examples of prophetic knowledge
The author cites several prophets: Muhammad, David, Solomon, Joseph, Lot, Moses, and Jacob. Each received judgment and knowledge directly from Allah.
For example, verse 4:113 mentions the Book and Wisdom taught to Muhammad.
3
Understand al-‘ilm al-ladunī
Al-Khidr possessed knowledge from Allah that even Prophet Moses did not know. This is called al-‘ilm al-ladunī, knowledge from God's presence.
Reference: Quran 18:65-66.
4
Understand iṣṭifā’
Iṣṭifā’ is a special teaching for righteous individuals, involving cultivation of good desires and weakening evil, increasing special revelation.
Its purpose is to present a model example for humanity.
5
State the purpose of iṣṭifā’
The purpose is to provide a role model for mankind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نظرية المعرفة بين القرآن والفلسفة مجموعة فعاليات ونشاطات كان للشعور والإرادة دخل في بعضها والبعض الآخر منها ناشئ من بعض الإلهامات والتعليم او التسديد كما يتجلى في القرآن الكريم على نوعين: -١ التعليم الالهي الخاص للنخبة من البشر وفي مقدمتهم الانبياء . أن الله أنزل على نبيه الكتاب والحكمة وعلمه ما لم يكن يعلم من قبل وَأَنْزَلَ اللهُ عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ وَالْحِكْمَةَ وَعَلَّمَكَ مَا لَمْ تَكُنْ تَعْلَمُ) (وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا دَاوُودَ وَسُلَيْمَانَ عِلْمًا وَقَالَا الْحَمْدُ لِلهِ الَّذِي فَضْلَنَا عَلَى كَثِيرٍ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ) وعن نبي الله يوسف قال تعالى (وَلَمَّا بَلَغَ أَشُدَّهُ آتَيْنَاهُ حُكْمًا وَعِلْمًا وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِي الْمُحْسِنِينَ) ؛ وعن نبي الله لوط قال تعالى (وَلُوطًا آتَيْنَاهُ حُكْمًا وَعِلْمًا) وعن نبي الله موسى قال تعالى (وَلَمَّا بَلَغَ أَشُدَّهُ وَاسْتَوَى آتَيْنَاهُ حُكْمًا وَعِلْمًا وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِي الْمُحْسِنِينَ) وفي قصة نبي الله موسى أن الخضر (وهو عبد صالح) لديه من العلم مما لا يعلمه النبي موسى نفسه وهذا النوع من العلم اصطلح على تسميته: العلم اللدني ويروى أن الخضر عليه السلام كان أشرف بني إسرائيل فكرمه الله بعلم خاص (فَوَجَدَا عَبْدًا مِنْ عِبَادِنَا آتَيْنَاهُ رَحْمَةً مِنْ عِنْدِنَا وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ مِنْ لَدُنَّا عِلْمًا، قَالَ لَهُ مُوسَى هَلْ أَتَّبِعُكَ عَلَى أَنْ تُعَلِّمَنِ مِمَّا عُلِّمْتَ رُشْدًا) وقد وصف نبي الله يعقوب في القرآن الكريم (وَإِنَّهُ لَذُو عِلْمٍ لِمَا عَلَّمْنَاهُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ النَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ) وهناك تعليم خاص لفئة من الصالحين يسمى الاصطفاء وهو تركيز الرغبات الخيرة في الفطرة السليمة وإضعاف الجانب الشرير من البصائر وزيادة في الوحي الخاص وكبح جماح العواطف في أماكن انطلاقها. إن الغاية من الاصطفاء هو تقديم الأنموذج القدوة لبني البشر. 
التعليم العام لبني البشر: أنموذجات من التعليم الإلهي
(١) الله علم الأسماء: قال تعالى (وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ الْأَسْمَاءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى الْمَلَائِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنْبِئُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ صَادِقِينَ) أي أسماء المسميات بدليل قوله (ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ) فالأسماء توقيفية وإن الله ذم قوماً على تسميتهم الأشياء من عند أنفسهم (إِنْ هِيَ إِلَّا أَسْمَاءٌ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَا أَنْتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ مَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ بِهَا مِنْ سُلْطَانٍ)
(٢) الله علم لغات العالم: وليس الزمن أو العادات (وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ خَلْقُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافُ أَلْسِنَتِكُمْ وَأَلْوَانِكُمْ إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِلْعَالِمِينَ) والمراد اختلاف اللغات وليس اختلاف الألسنة ابتداء اللغة وقع بالتعليم من الله سبحانه وتعالى والباقي يخترعه الإنسان من نفسه وهذه اللغة تتشعب بين أقوام متباعدة وتتطور بما يحدث فيها التغيير والزيادة فتنبثق لغات خاصة وهي هذه الأسماء التي يتعارف بها الناس إنسان ودابة وأرض وسهل
The theory of knowledge between the Quran and philosophy, a collection of activities and actions where consciousness and will had an input in some of them, and others arise from some inspirations and teaching or guidance, as manifested in the Noble Quran, is of two types: 1. The special divine teaching for an elite of mankind, foremost among them the prophets. God sent down to His Prophet the Book and Wisdom and taught him what he did not know before. 'And God sent down to you the Book and Wisdom and taught you what you did not know' (4:113). 'And We gave David and Solomon knowledge, and they said: Praise be to God Who has favored us above many of His believing servants' (27:15). And of the prophet of God Joseph, He said: 'And when he reached his maturity, We gave him judgment and knowledge, and thus We reward the doers of good' (12:22). And of the prophet of God Lot, He said: 'And Lot, We gave him judgment and knowledge' (21:74). And of the prophet of God Moses, He said: 'And when he reached his maturity and became established, We gave him judgment and knowledge, and thus We reward the doers of good' (28:14). And in the story of the prophet of God Moses, al-Khidr (a righteous servant) has knowledge that the prophet Moses himself did not know. This type of knowledge is conventionally called: al-‘ilm al-ladunī (knowledge from God's presence). And it is narrated that al-Khidr was the noblest of the Children of Israel, so God honored him with special knowledge: 'So they found a servant from among Our servants to whom We had given mercy from Ourselves and taught him knowledge from Our own presence. Moses said to him: May I follow you on condition that you teach me from what you have been taught of right guidance?' (18:65-66). And the prophet of God Jacob is described in the Noble Quran: 'And indeed he is a possessor of knowledge because of what We taught him, but most people do not know' (12:68). And there is a special teaching for a group of righteous people called al-iṣṭifā’ (selection), which is focusing the good desires in the sound innate disposition and weakening the evil aspect of insights and increasing in special revelation and restraining the emotions at their points of eruption. The purpose of al-iṣṭifā’ is to present the model example for mankind. The general teaching for mankind: examples of divine teaching. (1) God taught the names: He said: 'And He taught Adam the names, all of them; then He presented them to the angels and said: Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful' (2:31). That is, the names of the named things, as evidenced by His saying 'then He presented them'. So the names are Tawqīfī (revealed), and God blamed a people for naming things from themselves: 'They are but names which you have named, you and your fathers, for which God has sent down no authority' (53:23). (2) God taught the languages of the world: not time or customs. 'And among His signs are the creation of the heavens and the earth and the diversity of your languages and your colors. Indeed in that are signs for the worlds' (30:22). The meaning is the diversity of languages, not the diversity of tongues. The origin of language occurred by teaching from God Almighty, and the rest man invents from himself. This language branches out among distant nations and develops with changes and additions occurring in it, so special languages emerge, and these are the names by which people know each other: human, animal, land, plain.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage classifies divine teaching into two types: special and general, supported by Quranic evidence. The author begins by stating that the theory of knowledge in the Quran encompasses two categories. The first is special divine teaching reserved for an elite group, primarily the prophets. Numerous Quranic verses are cited to illustrate that Allah directly bestowed knowledge upon prophets such as Muhammad, David, Solomon, Joseph, Lot, Moses, and Jacob. A notable example is the knowledge given to al-Khidr, which exceeded even that of Prophet Moses, a type referred to as 'ilm ladunī (knowledge from God's presence). Additionally, there is a teaching for righteous individuals called iṣṭifā’ (selection), which involves cultivating good inclinations and subduing evil ones. The second type is general teaching for all humanity. The author provides two examples: Allah taught Adam all the names, indicating that names are divinely appointed (tawqīfī), and Allah created diverse languages, with the original language taught by God while humans later innovate and develop languages. The passage emphasizes that both special and general knowledge originate from divine instruction.

Key Terms
العلم اللدني
الاصطفاء
التعليم الإلهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the name of the type of knowledge that al-Khidr possessed according to the passage?
A) al-‘ilm al-ḥudūthī
B) al-‘ilm al-ladunī
C) al-‘ilm al-kasbī
D) al-‘ilm al-indī

Key Takeaway
Special divine teaching encompasses prophetic knowledge and iṣṭifā’, emphasizing that direct knowledge from God is a unique epistemological source.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a prophet from the passage who received special knowledge and cite the verse reference (e.g., Joseph: 12:22).
?
Explain the difference between prophetic knowledge and the iṣṭifā’ given to righteous individuals.

General Divine Teaching: The Origin of Names and Languages
Author classifies divine teaching into special and general types with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic view that the origin of names and languages is divine teaching, and identify the evidence provided.

Core Idea
Names and languages are originally taught by God, not invented by humans.

The Quran presents a second type of divine teaching: general teaching for all humanity. This lesson examines two examples: Allah teaching Adam all the names, and the diversity of languages as a sign from God. We will see how this establishes that the origin of language is divine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the examples of general divine teaching
The passage provides two examples: teaching Adam the names, and creating diversity of languages.
2
Analyze the teaching of names to Adam
Allah taught Adam the names of all things, then presented them to the angels. This indicates names are tawqīfī (revealed). The passage also cites a verse blaming those who name things without divine authority (53:23).
The phrase 'then He presented them' shows the names refer to the named entities.
3
Understand the diversity of languages
The verse 30:22 mentions diversity of languages as a sign. The author interprets this as languages taught by God initially, then humans innovate and develop them.
Linguistic diversity is thus a divine sign, not a result of mere human convention.
4
Conclude the role of divine teaching in language
The origin of language is divine teaching; humans later add and change, leading to multiple languages. This counters the idea that language is purely conventional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نظرية المعرفة بين القرآن والفلسفة مجموعة فعاليات ونشاطات كان للشعور والإرادة دخل في بعضها والبعض الآخر منها ناشئ من بعض الإلهامات والتعليم او التسديد كما يتجلى في القرآن الكريم على نوعين: -١ التعليم الالهي الخاص للنخبة من البشر وفي مقدمتهم الانبياء . أن الله أنزل على نبيه الكتاب والحكمة وعلمه ما لم يكن يعلم من قبل وَأَنْزَلَ اللهُ عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ وَالْحِكْمَةَ وَعَلَّمَكَ مَا لَمْ تَكُنْ تَعْلَمُ) (وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا دَاوُودَ وَسُلَيْمَانَ عِلْمًا وَقَالَا الْحَمْدُ لِلهِ الَّذِي فَضْلَنَا عَلَى كَثِيرٍ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ) وعن نبي الله يوسف قال تعالى (وَلَمَّا بَلَغَ أَشُدَّهُ آتَيْنَاهُ حُكْمًا وَعِلْمًا وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِي الْمُحْسِنِينَ) ؛ وعن نبي الله لوط قال تعالى (وَلُوطًا آتَيْنَاهُ حُكْمًا وَعِلْمًا) وعن نبي الله موسى قال تعالى (وَلَمَّا بَلَغَ أَشُدَّهُ وَاسْتَوَى آتَيْنَاهُ حُكْمًا وَعِلْمًا وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِي الْمُحْسِنِينَ) وفي قصة نبي الله موسى أن الخضر (وهو عبد صالح) لديه من العلم مما لا يعلمه النبي موسى نفسه وهذا النوع من العلم اصطلح على تسميته: العلم اللدني ويروى أن الخضر عليه السلام كان أشرف بني إسرائيل فكرمه الله بعلم خاص (فَوَجَدَا عَبْدًا مِنْ عِبَادِنَا آتَيْنَاهُ رَحْمَةً مِنْ عِنْدِنَا وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ مِنْ لَدُنَّا عِلْمًا، قَالَ لَهُ مُوسَى هَلْ أَتَّبِعُكَ عَلَى أَنْ تُعَلِّمَنِ مِمَّا عُلِّمْتَ رُشْدًا) وقد وصف نبي الله يعقوب في القرآن الكريم (وَإِنَّهُ لَذُو عِلْمٍ لِمَا عَلَّمْنَاهُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ النَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ) وهناك تعليم خاص لفئة من الصالحين يسمى الاصطفاء وهو تركيز الرغبات الخيرة في الفطرة السليمة وإضعاف الجانب الشرير من البصائر وزيادة في الوحي الخاص وكبح جماح العواطف في أماكن انطلاقها. إن الغاية من الاصطفاء هو تقديم الأنموذج القدوة لبني البشر. 
التعليم العام لبني البشر: أنموذجات من التعليم الإلهي
(١) الله علم الأسماء: قال تعالى (وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ الْأَسْمَاءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى الْمَلَائِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنْبِئُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ صَادِقِينَ) أي أسماء المسميات بدليل قوله (ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ) فالأسماء توقيفية وإن الله ذم قوماً على تسميتهم الأشياء من عند أنفسهم (إِنْ هِيَ إِلَّا أَسْمَاءٌ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَا أَنْتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ مَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ بِهَا مِنْ سُلْطَانٍ)
(٢) الله علم لغات العالم: وليس الزمن أو العادات (وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ خَلْقُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافُ أَلْسِنَتِكُمْ وَأَلْوَانِكُمْ إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِلْعَالِمِينَ) والمراد اختلاف اللغات وليس اختلاف الألسنة ابتداء اللغة وقع بالتعليم من الله سبحانه وتعالى والباقي يخترعه الإنسان من نفسه وهذه اللغة تتشعب بين أقوام متباعدة وتتطور بما يحدث فيها التغيير والزيادة فتنبثق لغات خاصة وهي هذه الأسماء التي يتعارف بها الناس إنسان ودابة وأرض وسهل
The theory of knowledge between the Quran and philosophy, a collection of activities and actions where consciousness and will had an input in some of them, and others arise from some inspirations and teaching or guidance, as manifested in the Noble Quran, is of two types: 1. The special divine teaching for an elite of mankind, foremost among them the prophets. God sent down to His Prophet the Book and Wisdom and taught him what he did not know before. 'And God sent down to you the Book and Wisdom and taught you what you did not know' (4:113). 'And We gave David and Solomon knowledge, and they said: Praise be to God Who has favored us above many of His believing servants' (27:15). And of the prophet of God Joseph, He said: 'And when he reached his maturity, We gave him judgment and knowledge, and thus We reward the doers of good' (12:22). And of the prophet of God Lot, He said: 'And Lot, We gave him judgment and knowledge' (21:74). And of the prophet of God Moses, He said: 'And when he reached his maturity and became established, We gave him judgment and knowledge, and thus We reward the doers of good' (28:14). And in the story of the prophet of God Moses, al-Khidr (a righteous servant) has knowledge that the prophet Moses himself did not know. This type of knowledge is conventionally called: al-‘ilm al-ladunī (knowledge from God's presence). And it is narrated that al-Khidr was the noblest of the Children of Israel, so God honored him with special knowledge: 'So they found a servant from among Our servants to whom We had given mercy from Ourselves and taught him knowledge from Our own presence. Moses said to him: May I follow you on condition that you teach me from what you have been taught of right guidance?' (18:65-66). And the prophet of God Jacob is described in the Noble Quran: 'And indeed he is a possessor of knowledge because of what We taught him, but most people do not know' (12:68). And there is a special teaching for a group of righteous people called al-iṣṭifā’ (selection), which is focusing the good desires in the sound innate disposition and weakening the evil aspect of insights and increasing in special revelation and restraining the emotions at their points of eruption. The purpose of al-iṣṭifā’ is to present the model example for mankind. The general teaching for mankind: examples of divine teaching. (1) God taught the names: He said: 'And He taught Adam the names, all of them; then He presented them to the angels and said: Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful' (2:31). That is, the names of the named things, as evidenced by His saying 'then He presented them'. So the names are Tawqīfī (revealed), and God blamed a people for naming things from themselves: 'They are but names which you have named, you and your fathers, for which God has sent down no authority' (53:23). (2) God taught the languages of the world: not time or customs. 'And among His signs are the creation of the heavens and the earth and the diversity of your languages and your colors. Indeed in that are signs for the worlds' (30:22). The meaning is the diversity of languages, not the diversity of tongues. The origin of language occurred by teaching from God Almighty, and the rest man invents from himself. This language branches out among distant nations and develops with changes and additions occurring in it, so special languages emerge, and these are the names by which people know each other: human, animal, land, plain.

Commentary
This passage classifies divine teaching into two types: special and general, supported by Quranic evidence. The author begins by stating that the theory of knowledge in the Quran encompasses two categories. The first is special divine teaching reserved for an elite group, primarily the prophets. Numerous Quranic verses are cited to illustrate that Allah directly bestowed knowledge upon prophets such as Muhammad, David, Solomon, Joseph, Lot, Moses, and Jacob. A notable example is the knowledge given to al-Khidr, which exceeded even that of Prophet Moses, a type referred to as 'ilm ladunī (knowledge from God's presence). Additionally, there is a teaching for righteous individuals called iṣṭifā’ (selection), which involves cultivating good inclinations and subduing evil ones. The second type is general teaching for all humanity. The author provides two examples: Allah taught Adam all the names, indicating that names are divinely appointed (tawqīfī), and Allah created diverse languages, with the original language taught by God while humans later innovate and develop languages. The passage emphasizes that both special and general knowledge originate from divine instruction.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the significance of the verse 'And He taught Adam the names, all of them' (2:31)?
A) It shows that names are arbitrary conventions
B) It proves that names are divinely taught

Key Takeaway
General divine teaching includes the origin of names and languages, affirming that fundamental human knowledge of naming and language comes from God.

Divine Origin of Language Diversity
Author asserts divine origin of language diversity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the claim about the divine origin of language diversity and explain its epistemological basis.

Core Idea
Language diversity is rooted in divine teaching.

This passage presents a theological account of the origin of language diversity. You will learn how the author uses religious narrations to ground the multiplicity of languages in divine action, and what this implies for the nature of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the observable cause
The author starts by acknowledging that human diversity in tastes, environment, and lifestyles leads to language diversity. This is the empirical observation.
2
Locate the religious claim
Then, the author cites religious narrations saying God taught Adam seventy-two languages. This is the theological anchor.
3
Note the reduction to four origins
The passage further claims that these seventy-two languages originate from just four primary languages, from which all others branch.
4
Assess epistemological status
Consider: Is this presented as a proof or a narrative? The author relies on religious narrations, not rational argument. This marks the epistemological stance: knowledge comes from revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبحر وجبل وحمار وأشباه ذلك من الأمم وغيرها، لا شك أن البشر متنوعون في الأذواق وفي البيئة وفي أنماط الحياة وبسبب ذلك تنوعت لغاتهم واختلفت وتقول الروايات الدينية أن الله تعالى علم آدم اثنتين وسبعين لغة وهي أصول لغات العالم، وهذه اللغات أصلها أربع فقط ومنها تتشعب بقية اللغات كلها حتى تصل إلى العدد الموجود اليوم.
And sea, mountain, donkey, and similar from the nations and others. No doubt that humans are diverse in tastes, environment, and lifestyles, and due to that their languages diversified and differed. Religious narrations say that God Almighty taught Adam seventy-two languages, and they are the origins of the world's languages. These languages have only four origins, and from them all the rest of the languages branch until reaching the number existing today.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological claim about the origin of human languages. It begins by acknowledging the observable diversity of human tastes, environments, and lifestyles, which leads to language diversity. The author then cites religious narrations (روايات دينية) to assert that God directly taught Adam seventy-two languages, which are the roots of all world languages. Furthermore, it claims that these seventy-two originate from just four primary languages, from which all others branch. This is not a formal argument but a statement of belief in divine origin of language, situating knowledge within a theological framework.

Key Terms
الروايات الدينية (al-riwāyāt al-dīniyya): Religious narrations
أصول لغات العالم (uṣūl lughāt al-ʿālam): The original root languages of the world

Key Takeaway

Knowledge as Divine Teaching: Tracing All Human Learnings to God
Author enumerates examples of divine teaching across crafts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the common epistemological argument in the author's enumeration of crafts and evaluate its use of Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Every human craft and discovery ultimately originates from divine teaching, not mere trial.

In this passage, the author argues that all knowledge—from writing to agriculture—is ultimately taught by God. By citing Quranic verses for each craft, he establishes a pattern: God is the teacher of even the most practical skills. This lesson will help you parse this argument and see how it functions in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching thesis
Read the opening and closing paragraphs. What is the author's central claim? It is that all knowledge originates from God's teaching, either directly or through inspiration.
2
List the enumerated crafts and their verses
Find the five crafts: writing, armor making, hunting with trained animals, ironworking, and agriculture. For each, note the Quranic verse cited. Observe how each verse directly attributes the skill to God.
3
Analyze the agriculture example
The author acknowledges experiential learning but insists that the original knowledge is from God. Notice the rhetorical question: 'Do you grow it, or are We the grower?' This counters the objection that agriculture is purely empirical.
4
Extend to inventors and inspiration
The final paragraph generalizes: inventors attribute breakthroughs to inspiration received in states of unawareness (dreams, walks). This reinforces the thesis that even seemingly self-derived discoveries come from God.
The author uses ilhām in a broad sense here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتابة من تعليم الله: قال تعالى (وَلَا يَأْبَ كَاتِبٌ أَنْ يَكْتُبَ كَمَا عَلَّمَهُ اللَّهُ فَلْيَكْتُبْ). (ه) تعليم فن صناعة الدرع قال تعالى (وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ صَنْعَةَ لَبُوسٍ لَكُمْ لِتُحْصِنَكُمْ مِنْ بَأْسِكُمْ فَهَلْ أَنْتُمْ شَاكِرُونَ). (٦) تعليم حيوانات الصيد قال تعالى (وَمَا عَلَّمْتُمْ مِنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَذِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللَّهُ). (۷) تعليم صناعة الحديد: قال تعالى (وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا دَاوُودَ مِنَّا فَضْلًا يَا جِبَالُ أَوِّبِي مَعَهُ وَالطَّيْرَ وَأَلَنَّا لَهُ الْحَدِيدَ أَنِ اعْمَلْ سَابِغَاتٍ وَقَدِّرْ فِي السَّرْدِ وَاعْمَلُوا صَالِحًا إِنِّي بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ). (۸) تعليم الزراعة: قد يتعلم الإنسان كيفية الزراعة عن طريق التجربة لكن هذه التجربة ليس أصل الزراعة الذي تعلمه الإنسان من الله (وَلَقَدْ عَلِمْتُمُ النَّشْأَةَ الْأُولَى فَلَوْلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ أَفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَا تَحْرُثُونَ أَأَنْتُمْ تَزْرَعُونَهُ أَمْ نَحْنُ الزَّارِعُونَ). لاحظوا أيها السادة القراء الأعزاء أن جل المكتشفين والمخترعين إن لم يكن كلهم قالوا بأن العامل الجوهري لمنجزاتهم العلمية هو ما ألهموا به من أمور وهم في غفلة وعدم اشتغال بالكشف والاختبار كأن يكون أحدهم في حالة منام أو في أثناء المشي في متنزه أو ما شابه بعد أن يئسوا أو كادوا ييأسون.
Writing is from God's teaching: He said, Most High: 'And let not the writer refuse to write as God has taught him, so let him write.' (H) Teaching the art of armor making: He said, Most High: 'And We taught him the making of coats of armor for you, to protect you from your [enemy's] assault. So will you be grateful?' (6) Teaching hunting animals: He said, Most High: 'And what you have taught of hunting animals [to catch] ... teaching them from what God has taught you.' (7) Teaching ironworking: He said, Most High: 'And indeed We gave David from Our bounty: O mountains, repeat [the name of God] with him, and the birds. And We made iron soft for him. Work on suits of chain mail and measure the links, and do righteousness. Indeed I am seeing what you do.' (8) Teaching agriculture: Man may learn how to cultivate through experience, but that experience is not the origin of agriculture; what man learned from God is the origin. And indeed you have known the first creation, so will you not remember? Have you considered what you cultivate? Do you grow it, or are We the grower? Note, dear dear readers, that most discoverers and inventors, if not all of them, said that the essential factor for their scientific achievements is what they were inspired with while in a state of unawareness and not engaged in discovery and testing – such as one of them being in a dream or while walking in a park or the like, after they had despaired or almost despaired.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of several types of knowledge that the author argues come from divine teaching. Each is supported by a Quranic verse: writing (2:282), armor making (21:80), hunting with trained animals (5:4), ironworking (34:10-11), and agriculture (56:62-64). For agriculture, the author acknowledges experiential learning but insists that the original knowledge was from God. The final paragraph generalizes: most inventors and discoverers attribute their breakthroughs to inspiration received in states of passivity (dreams, walking, etc.) after despair. Thus, the passage asserts that all human knowledge ultimately originates from God, either through direct teaching or inspiration.

الإلهام

A) Pure human experience
B) Trial and error
C) Divine teaching from God

Key Takeaway
All human knowledge, from the simplest craft to the greatest invention, ultimately owes its origin to divine teaching or inspiration.

Types of Divine Teaching in the Quran
Author lists Quranic examples of divine teaching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the types of divine teaching (ta'leem) mentioned in the Quran with their corresponding verses.

Core Idea
The Quran presents practical arts as direct divine teaching, not human invention.

In this passage, the author lists several examples of divine teaching from the Quran, including writing, armor-making, training hunting animals, ironworking, and agriculture. Each example is supported by a verse that attributes the origin of the skill to God. This lesson will guide you through identifying these types and understanding how the author uses them to argue that divine teaching is a primary source of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the examples of divine teaching
Locate each example in the Arabic passage: writing, armor-making, hunting animal training, ironworking, and agriculture. Note the Quranic verses cited for each.
2
Extract the Quranic evidence
For each example, read the verse as quoted. Notice that the author interprets these verses as demonstrating direct divine instruction, not human discovery.
3
Analyze the author's argument
The author claims that inventors and discoverers often receive inspiration in states of unawareness (e.g., dreams, walks) after despair, yet some arrogantly attribute it to themselves. How does this support his thesis?
4
Summarize the classification
List the five types of teaching and their Quranic references. This classification shows that practical arts are divinely taught, forming a source of knowledge.

الكتابة من تعليم الله : قال تعالى (وَلَا يَاب كاتب أن يكتب كَمَا عَلَمَهُ الله فَلْيَكتب) تعليم فن صناعة الدرع قال تعالى (وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ صَنْعَةَ لَبُوسِ لَكُمْ لِتُحْصِنَكُمْ مِنْ بَأْسِكُمْ فَهَلْ أَنتُمْ شَاكِرُونَ) تعليم حيوانات الصيد قال تعالى (وَمَا عَلَّمْتُمْ مِنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَذِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللهُ) تعليم صناعة الحديد: قال تعالى (وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا دَاوُودَ مِنَّا فَضْلًا يَا جِبَالُ أوبي مَعَهُ وَالطَّيْرَ وَأَلَنَّا لَهُ الْحَدِيدَ . أَنِ اعْمَلَ سَابِغَاتِ وَقَدْرْ فِي السِّرْدِ وَاعْمَلُوا صَالِحًا إِنِّي بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ) تعليم الزراعة : قد يتعلم الانسان كيفية الزراعة عن طريق التجربة لكن هذه التجربة ليس أصل الزراعة الذي تعلمه الانسان من الله (وَلَقَدْ عَلِمْتُمُ النشأَةَ الْأُولَى فَلَوْلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ أفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَا تَحرثُونَ . أَأَنتُم تَزْرَعُونَهُ أمْ نَحْنُ الزّارِعُونَ) لاحظوا ايها السادة القراء الاعزاء ان جل المكتشفين والمخترعين ان لم يكن كلهم قالوا بأن العامل الجوهري لمنجزاتهم العلمية هو ما ألهموا به من أمور وهم في غفلة وعدم اشتغال بالكشف والاختبار كأن يكون أحدهم في حالة منام أو في أثناء المشي في متنزه أو ما شابه بعد أن يئسوا أو كادوا ييأسون ولكن قسما من هؤلاء بقوا مكابرين فنسبوا هذه المخترعات الى أنفسهم وسكتوا عن الاشارة الى دور الفيض الالهي في معرفتهم. قال الشاعر على المرء ان يبذل قصارى جهده وليس عليه أن يكون موفقا وقال آخر (أنت الذي نال الكمال موفقاً ... من رازق من شاء غير محاسب) وقال كعب بن مالك يصف النبي محمد - ص - إذا كان منه القول كان موفقاً ... وإن كان حياً كان نوراً مجددا ان الفرق بين التعليم والهداية ان الهداية تختص بأمرين هما هداية في امور اداء الخلقة التكوينية وهي مستمرة زمانيا طول حياة الكائن الحي وهداية في أمور الاعتقاد تقود صاحبها الى الفوز او الخسارة . أما التعليم فهو تسديد لتطوير علوم الحياة من صناعة وزراعة ولغة وغيرها . الخلاصة : ان التعليم هو تسديد الهي للانسان يمكن تمثيله بأشراقة روحية للحظات من الزمن تخص الامور الجوهرية ويعد واحدا من مصادر المعرفة في نظرية القرآن الكريم.
Writing is from the teaching of God: He said, 'And let the scribe not refuse to write as God has taught him, so let him write.' Teaching the art of making armor: He said, 'And We taught him the making of coats of mail for you, to protect you from your violence; then are you grateful?' Teaching hunting animals: He said, 'And those you have trained of hunting animals, teaching them as God has taught you.' Teaching the working of iron: He said, 'And We certainly gave David from Us bounty: O mountains, repeat praise with him, and the birds; and We made iron soft for him. Work, O family of David, in gratitude.' Teaching agriculture: Man may learn how to cultivate by experience, but this experience is not the origin of agriculture which man learned from God, 'And you have already known the first creation, so will you not remember? Have you seen what you cultivate? Do you cultivate it, or are We the cultivators?' Note, dear readers, that most discoverers and inventors, if not all, said that the essential factor in their scientific achievements is what they were inspired with while unaware and not engaged in discovery and testing, such as being in a dream or while walking in a park or the like, after they despaired or almost despaired. But a portion of them remained obstinate, attributing these inventions to themselves and remaining silent about pointing to the role of divine emanation in their knowledge. The poet said: 'Man must exert his utmost effort, and it is not upon him to be successful.' Another said: 'You who attained perfection successfully... from a Provider who gives to whomever He wills without reckoning.' And Ka'b ibn Malik said describing the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him): 'When he spoke, he was successful... And if he was living, he was a renewed light.' The difference between teaching and guidance is that guidance pertains to two matters: guidance in the matters of performing the natural constitution, which is continuous temporally throughout the life of the living being, and guidance in matters of belief, leading its possessor to success or loss. As for teaching, it is divine direction for the development of the sciences of life, such as industry, agriculture, language, and others. Conclusion: Teaching is divine direction for man, which can be represented as a spiritual illumination for moments of time concerning essential matters, and it is considered one of the sources of knowledge in the theory of the Noble Quran.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents an epistemological argument from a Quranic perspective, classifying divine teaching (تعليم) as a fundamental source of knowledge. The author, likely Sheikh Abd al-Zahra Turki al-Fatlawi, enumerates several types of teaching explicitly mentioned in the Quran: writing, armor-making, training hunting animals, ironworking, and agriculture. For each, he cites a relevant verse, emphasizing that the origin of these arts is not human invention but divine instruction. He then observes that most inventors and discoverers attribute their breakthroughs to inspiration received in states of unawareness, such as during dreams or walks, after despair. However, some arrogantly claim credit for themselves, ignoring the divine influx (فيض إلهي). The author distinguishes teaching (تعليم) from guidance (هداية): guidance is continuous and pertains to natural constitution and belief, while teaching is specific, momentary illumination for developing life sciences. The conclusion reinforces that teaching is a divine 'sustaining' (تسديد) that constitutes a source of knowledge in the Quranic worldview. This passage does not construct a formal logical argument but rather classifies and explains using Quranic evidence.

Key Terms
تعليم
هداية
تسديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Divine teaching is a distinct source of knowledge in the Quran, encompassing practical arts and sciences.

Distinguishing Divine Teaching from Guidance
Author distinguishes teaching from guidance with definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between divine teaching (ta'leem) and guidance (hidayah) according to the author's criteria.

Core Idea
Teaching is momentary inspiration; guidance is continuous direction.

The passage concludes with a clear distinction between teaching and guidance. Guidance is continuous and covers natural constitution and belief, while teaching is temporary and focused on developing worldly sciences. This lesson will help you apply this distinction and understand its implications for Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Locate the distinction in the passage
Find the sentence: 'ان الفرق بين التعليم والهداية ان الهداية تختص بأمرين...' and read the paragraph that follows.
2
Identify the two aspects of guidance
The author divides guidance into two types: one related to natural constitution (continuous over a lifetime) and one related to belief (leading to success or loss). Note these.
3
Define teaching according to the author
Teaching is described as 'تسديد لتطوير علوم الحياة' (divine direction for developing life sciences) and as a 'spiritual illumination for moments of time'. Contrast this with the continuity of guidance.
4
Apply the distinction to a new example
Consider the skill of writing: is it an example of teaching or guidance? According to the author, it is teaching because it is a learned art, not a natural constitution or belief.

الكتابة من تعليم الله : قال تعالى (وَلَا يَاب كاتب أن يكتب كَمَا عَلَمَهُ الله فَلْيَكتب) تعليم فن صناعة الدرع قال تعالى (وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ صَنْعَةَ لَبُوسِ لَكُمْ لِتُحْصِنَكُمْ مِنْ بَأْسِكُمْ فَهَلْ أَنتُمْ شَاكِرُونَ) تعليم حيوانات الصيد قال تعالى (وَمَا عَلَّمْتُمْ مِنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَذِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللهُ) تعليم صناعة الحديد: قال تعالى (وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا دَاوُودَ مِنَّا فَضْلًا يَا جِبَالُ أوبي مَعَهُ وَالطَّيْرَ وَأَلَنَّا لَهُ الْحَدِيدَ . أَنِ اعْمَلَ سَابِغَاتِ وَقَدْرْ فِي السِّرْدِ وَاعْمَلُوا صَالِحًا إِنِّي بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ) تعليم الزراعة : قد يتعلم الانسان كيفية الزراعة عن طريق التجربة لكن هذه التجربة ليس أصل الزراعة الذي تعلمه الانسان من الله (وَلَقَدْ عَلِمْتُمُ النشأَةَ الْأُولَى فَلَوْلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ أفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَا تَحرثُونَ . أَأَنتُم تَزْرَعُونَهُ أمْ نَحْنُ الزّارِعُونَ) لاحظوا ايها السادة القراء الاعزاء ان جل المكتشفين والمخترعين ان لم يكن كلهم قالوا بأن العامل الجوهري لمنجزاتهم العلمية هو ما ألهموا به من أمور وهم في غفلة وعدم اشتغال بالكشف والاختبار كأن يكون أحدهم في حالة منام أو في أثناء المشي في متنزه أو ما شابه بعد أن يئسوا أو كادوا ييأسون ولكن قسما من هؤلاء بقوا مكابرين فنسبوا هذه المخترعات الى أنفسهم وسكتوا عن الاشارة الى دور الفيض الالهي في معرفتهم. قال الشاعر على المرء ان يبذل قصارى جهده وليس عليه أن يكون موفقا وقال آخر (أنت الذي نال الكمال موفقاً ... من رازق من شاء غير محاسب) وقال كعب بن مالك يصف النبي محمد - ص - إذا كان منه القول كان موفقاً ... وإن كان حياً كان نوراً مجددا ان الفرق بين التعليم والهداية ان الهداية تختص بأمرين هما هداية في امور اداء الخلقة التكوينية وهي مستمرة زمانيا طول حياة الكائن الحي وهداية في أمور الاعتقاد تقود صاحبها الى الفوز او الخسارة . أما التعليم فهو تسديد لتطوير علوم الحياة من صناعة وزراعة ولغة وغيرها . الخلاصة : ان التعليم هو تسديد الهي للانسان يمكن تمثيله بأشراقة روحية للحظات من الزمن تخص الامور الجوهرية ويعد واحدا من مصادر المعرفة في نظرية القرآن الكريم.
Writing is from the teaching of God: He said, 'And let the scribe not refuse to write as God has taught him, so let him write.' Teaching the art of making armor: He said, 'And We taught him the making of coats of mail for you, to protect you from your violence; then are you grateful?' Teaching hunting animals: He said, 'And those you have trained of hunting animals, teaching them as God has taught you.' Teaching the working of iron: He said, 'And We certainly gave David from Us bounty: O mountains, repeat praise with him, and the birds; and We made iron soft for him. Work, O family of David, in gratitude.' Teaching agriculture: Man may learn how to cultivate by experience, but this experience is not the origin of agriculture which man learned from God, 'And you have already known the first creation, so will you not remember? Have you seen what you cultivate? Do you cultivate it, or are We the cultivators?' Note, dear readers, that most discoverers and inventors, if not all, said that the essential factor in their scientific achievements is what they were inspired with while unaware and not engaged in discovery and testing, such as being in a dream or while walking in a park or the like, after they despaired or almost despaired. But a portion of them remained obstinate, attributing these inventions to themselves and remaining silent about pointing to the role of divine emanation in their knowledge. The poet said: 'Man must exert his utmost effort, and it is not upon him to be successful.' Another said: 'You who attained perfection successfully... from a Provider who gives to whomever He wills without reckoning.' And Ka'b ibn Malik said describing the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him): 'When he spoke, he was successful... And if he was living, he was a renewed light.' The difference between teaching and guidance is that guidance pertains to two matters: guidance in the matters of performing the natural constitution, which is continuous temporally throughout the life of the living being, and guidance in matters of belief, leading its possessor to success or loss. As for teaching, it is divine direction for the development of the sciences of life, such as industry, agriculture, language, and others. Conclusion: Teaching is divine direction for man, which can be represented as a spiritual illumination for moments of time concerning essential matters, and it is considered one of the sources of knowledge in the theory of the Noble Quran.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents an epistemological argument from a Quranic perspective, classifying divine teaching (تعليم) as a fundamental source of knowledge. The author, likely Sheikh Abd al-Zahra Turki al-Fatlawi, enumerates several types of teaching explicitly mentioned in the Quran: writing, armor-making, training hunting animals, ironworking, and agriculture. For each, he cites a relevant verse, emphasizing that the origin of these arts is not human invention but divine instruction. He then observes that most inventors and discoverers attribute their breakthroughs to inspiration received in states of unawareness, such as during dreams or walks, after despair. However, some arrogantly claim credit for themselves, ignoring the divine influx (فيض إلهي). The author distinguishes teaching (تعليم) from guidance (هداية): guidance is continuous and pertains to natural constitution and belief, while teaching is specific, momentary illumination for developing life sciences. The conclusion reinforces that teaching is a divine 'sustaining' (تسديد) that constitutes a source of knowledge in the Quranic worldview. This passage does not construct a formal logical argument but rather classifies and explains using Quranic evidence.

Key Terms
تعليم
هداية
تسديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a characteristic of guidance (هداية) but not of teaching (تعليم)?
A) It is momentary
B) It pertains to life sciences
C) It is continuous temporally
D) It comes as a spiritual illumination

Key Takeaway
Guidance is continuous and covers constitution and belief; teaching is momentary inspiration for worldly sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Categorize the following as either teaching or guidance according to the author: a) a baby's instinct to suckle, b) learning a trade like carpentry, c) belief in Tawhid. Explain your reasoning.
?
Write a short paragraph explaining how the author's definition of teaching as 'spiritual illumination for moments of time' relates to the experience of inventors mentioned earlier in the passage.

Dreams as a Source of Knowledge
Author introduces dreams as a source of knowledge with definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the physiological and spiritual interpretations of sleep in the Islamic epistemological framework.

Core Idea
Dreams bridge the physiological and the divine, making them a unique source of knowledge.

The passage introduces dreams as a source of knowledge, presenting two complementary interpretations of sleep—one from medicine and one from revelation. This sets the stage for understanding how Islamic thought integrates empirical and spiritual sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations
Find the two explanations of sleep given in the passage: one based on physiology (relaxation of brain nerves) and one based on revelation (God taking the soul without death).
2
Contrast the explanations
Compare the physiological cause (vapors rising to the brain) with the spiritual cause (divine soul-taking). Note that both are presented as valid from different perspectives.
3
Analyze the scriptural support
Examine the Quranic verse (Az-Zumar 42) cited: 'God takes the souls at the time of their death, and those that die not during their sleep.' How does this verse support the spiritual interpretation?
4
Consider the epistemological implication
If sleep involves a partial separation of the soul, then during that state, the soul may receive knowledge directly from God. This makes dreams a potential source of knowledge.
5
Reflect on the dual perspective
Why does the author say both interpretations are 'correct' (صحيح) though different? This reflects the Islamic tradition's openness to both empirical and revealed knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرؤيا المنامية النوم فسر على أوجه كلها صحيح بنظرات مختلفة : قيل هو استرخاء أعصاب الدماغ برطوبات البخار الصاعد إليه وقيل هو ان يتوفى الله النفس من غير موت اللهُ يَتَوَفَّى الْأَنْفُسَ حِينَ مَوتِهَا وَالَّتِي لَمْ تَمُتْ فِي مَنَامِهَا فَيُمْسِكَ الَّتِي قَضَى عَلَيْهَا الْمَوْتَ وَيُرْسِلُ الْأَخْرَى إِلَى أَجَلٍ مُسَمَّى (الله)
The dream vision. Sleep is interpreted in ways, all correct with different perspectives: It is said it is the relaxation of the nerves of the brain by the vapors rising to it, and it is said it is that God takes the soul without death: 'God takes the souls at the time of their death, and those that die not during their sleep; then He keeps those for which He has decreed death and releases the others for a specified term.'
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on dream visions (الرؤيا المنامية) as a source of knowledge. The author presents two interpretations of sleep: a physiological one (relaxation of brain nerves due to rising vapors) and a spiritual one (God taking the soul temporarily, citing Quran 39:42). This dual perspective allows dreams to be considered a conduit for divine knowledge. The passage is introductory; it does not elaborate on the epistemological status of dreams but sets the stage for later discussion. No formal argument is presented here, just a definition and a scriptural reference.

Key Terms
الرؤيا المنامية
النوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Surah Al-Baqarah 282

Key Takeaway
The passage presents two valid interpretations of sleep—physiological and spiritual—allowing dreams to serve as a bridge between natural processes and divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
